12:30 p.m. - Standard Overview
------------------------------


*by Jacob van Lunen* 

The Standard metagame has become colorful and diverse since the banning of [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor), and [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic), and the introduction of ***Magic** 2012*. We're looking forward to the new and exciting tech from the pros here at Grand Prix Pittsburgh, but what are the decks that they're aiming to beat?


Let's take a look at some of the big contenders in today's Standard metagame.







#### Caw Go - Designed by Gerry Thompson


##### 






![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

Blue-White [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Squadron+Hawk) decks has been the menace of the format for quite some time now. Many high level players have reportedly gone the way of Gerry and dropped the swords from their lists. The deck is resilient and powerful: It can be aggressive when it needs to be, it has a brilliant suite of disruption, and, with optimal draws, it can out-last even the most controlling builds of Blue-Black. This is certainly the deck to beat coming into this event.







#### Splinter Twin - Designed by Anders Simpson-Wolf


##### 






![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

75 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Mountain)


















A lot of people had thought that [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) was dead and gone before the Star City Games Open in Boston last weekend... but the recent uprising of [Valakut, the Molten Pinnacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Valakut%252C%2Bthe%2BMolten%2BPinnacle) and Eldrazi Green strategies has paved the way for [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) to make a big splash in Standard. Anders Simspon-Wolf combed his way to the top, in an event that featured a total of 6 Blue-Red [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Splinter%2BTwin) decks in the Top 16.


The deck combos [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch) with [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) to make an arbitrarily large number of 1/4s and attack its opponent for billions of damage. The library manipulation provided by [Shrine of Piercing Vision](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Shrine+of+Piercing+Vision), [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder), [Gitaxian Probe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gitaxian+Probe), and [Halimar Depths](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Halimar+Depths) allows [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) to find its combo, and the counterpells that it needs to go off safely. Expect [Dismember](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dismember) to become more popular again this weekend as a reaction to [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin)'s recent successes.







#### Mono-Red () - Designed by Anders Simpson-Wolf

Mono-Red has been able to survive and thrive even under the oppression of [Timely Reinforcements](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Timely+Reinforcements). Recent **Magic** Online daily events have been getting crushed by the Goblin based version of the deck. Red decks have adapted to playing against [Timely Reinforcements](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Timely+Reinforcements) by played cards like Chandra's Pheonix and [Hero of Oxid Ridge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hero+of+Oxid+Ridge).

75 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Forest)


















[Valakut, the Molten Pinnacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Valakut%252C%2Bthe%2BMolten%2BPinnacle) has made a resurgence due to it's remarkable strength against decks like Blue Black control and [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Squadron%2BHawk) [Sword of Feast and Famine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Sword%2Bof%2BFeast%2Band%2BFamine). The deck uses [Primeval Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Primeval+Titan) to search up a pile of mountains alongside a few [Valakut, the Molten Pinnacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Valakut%2C+the+Molten+Pinnacle). The deck has a raw power level and consistency that's very hard to match. Cards like [Summoning Trap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Summoning+Trap) make it difficult to profitably counter key creatures while cards like [Oracle of Mul Daya](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oracle+of+Mul+Daya) provide an excellent stream of card advantage. [Valakut, the Molten Pinnacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Valakut%252C%2Bthe%2BMolten%2BPinnacle) is powerful, but the recent success of [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) may scare a lot of players away from it.







#### Blue Black Control - Designed by Ali Aintrazi


#####

75 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Mystifying+Maze)


















Blue-Black control is a nightmare matchup for most creature heavy decks. The deck plays a lot of situationally strong, and interactive cards alongside library manipulation like [Preordain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Preordain), and card advantageous spells like [Jace Beleren](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace+Beleren). [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek), [Despise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Despise), and [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak) provide disruption and give the deck a chance against combo. The deck has proven itself to have an edge against many versions of [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Squadron%2BHawk) [Sword of Feast and Famine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Sword%2Bof%2BFeast%2Band%2BFamine). This deck is a powerful reactive tool that can be very dangerous in the hands of a skilled player.

[Garruk Wildspeaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BGarruk%5D+%5BWildspeaker%5D)

[Green Sun's Zenith](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BGreen%5D+%5BSun%5D+%5BZenith%5D)


2
[Karn Liberated](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BKarn%5D+%5BLiberated%5D)


75 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Khalni+Garden)


















Mono Green Eldrazi uses mana producing creatures and lands like [Eye of Ugin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Eye+of+Ugin) and [Eldrazi Temple](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Eldrazi+Temple) to cast gigantic Eldrazi Monsters like [Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Emrakul%2C+the+Aeons+Torn). If you enjoy casting fifteen mana cost creatures on your sixth turn, then this is certainly your cup of tea. The deck is very strong against control decks, but it lacks strength against combo and Mono Red. The recent inclusion of [Fauna Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fauna+Shaman) and [Spellskite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spellskite) allow savvy Mono-Green Eldrazi players to have a fighting chance against their worst matchup, [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin).


There will be a lot of new technology floating around here at Grand Prix: Pittsburgh. Stay tuned to find out what innovative decks make it to the top tables here on Day 1!




Saturday, 12:45 p.m. - Grand Prix Pittsburgh the Third
------------------------------------------------------


*by Steve Sadin* 

This weekend mark the third time that Pittsburgh has hosted a Grand Prix. The first Grand Prix Pittsburgh took place in 2000, a **Mercadian Masques** Block Team Limited event with a star-studded Top 4 featuring team "Antarctica"– Jon Finkel (at the height of his powers), Steve OMS (who was recently voted into the Hall of Fame), and Dan OMS.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppit11/Antarctica.jpg)Joining Antarctica in the Top 4, was team "Your Move Games"– Darwin Kastle, Dave "Da Hump" Humphreys, and Rob Dougherty. The Boston trio (who are now all in the Hall of Fame) was just a few months removed from winning the inaugural Team Pro Tour in Washington D.C. and were considered heavy favorites going into the event.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppit11/YMG.jpg)  
  

  
 However, the tournament was ultimately won by "Huey, Ben, and Casey"– a squad comprised of Hall of Famer Ben Rubin, four-time Pro Tour Top 8 competitor William "Huey" Jensen (who later captained the only team to beat Kai Budde in a Team Pro Tour Top 4), and Pro Tour New York 1999 champion Casey McCarrel.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppit11/Huey%20Ben%20and%20Casey.jpg)In 2003 Grand Prix Pittsburgh gave players a chance to show off their skills at *Onslaught* Block Team Limited. While the Top 4 of the second Grand Prix Pittsburgh wasn't as pro-laden as the first, it was nonetheless won by the Team Limited powerhouse team "Illuminati" which consisted of Pro Tour Tokyo 2001 champion, and master deck designer Zvi Mowshowitz, Pro Tour New Orelans 2003 champion Justin Gary, and 21 time Grand Prix Top 8 competitor Alex Shvartsman.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppit11/Illuminati.jpg)  
  

  
 In the finals, the Your Move Games Illuminati defeated a team captained by a young, and virtually unknown, Charles Gindy. Gindy would go on to become one of only a handful of players to win a Grand Prix, a Pro Tour, and Nationals.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppit11/Young%20Gindy.jpg)A little over 8 years later, and 1435 players from all over the world have shown up to play in one of the final pre-*Innistrad* Standard events. Up for grabs is $30,000, hundreds of highly coveted Pro Points, 16 invitations to Pro Tour Dark Ascension in Honolulu, and the title of Grand Prix Pittsburgh Champion.


Will a globetrotting pro on his way to Pro Tour Philly walk away with the title? Or will a hometown hero such as Grand Prix Minneapolis champ Zohar Bhagat, or Vintage mastermind Rich Shay keep the trophy in the Steel City?


Stay tuned to find out!




Saturday, 1:45 p.m. - In for the Long Haul
------------------------------------------


*by Nate Price* 

For those of you who don't know, there is a Pro Tour going on next weekend a few hundred miles down I-76 in Philadelphia. Wizards has a tendency to have Grand Prix in a similar part of the world to upcoming Pro Tour in the week prior, like having Grand Prix Singapore before Pro Tour Nagoya earlier this year. Whenever that happens, many pros jump on the opportunity to head to both tournaments in one fell swoop.


"It's like a free Grand Prix for me," Czech supertar Martin Juza explained. "I save a lot of money on flights and get an extra tournament in on my trip."


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppit11/juza.jpg)Because of this, there are often a larger concentration of Pro players at these events than in other Grand Prix. You also get a larger section of the global Pro community than you normally would. It's nice to see some of the bigger names in **Magic**, names that you only really see at Pro Tours or at Grand Prix in their local region, getting out and playing **Magic** at the Grand Prix level around the world. I'm not talking about players like Juza, Shuhei Nakamura, Brian Kibler, or Paulo Vitor Damo da Rosa. These guys are already fairly famous for their globetrotting for Grand Prix, heading anywhere they can sleeve up some cardboard for a game. I'm talking about players like Simon Görtzen, who rarely heads out of Europe for non-Pro Tour events. Players like Robert Jurkovic and Matej "The Big Z" Zatlkaj from Slovakia, who are big names on the Pro Tour that are rarely seen here around the United States. I'm talking Olle "I'm riding on the back of a giant freaking spider" Rade, Hall of Famer and the winner of the first **Magic** Invitational. These are players that are institutions in the global game that many of the players from outside their home areas just simply are unfamiliar with.


"I really think it's great for Wizards and for the community, too," revealed Juza. "Since so many of the Pros are going to make the trip for both, it gives the local players a chance to interact and maybe even play against the Pro players, which can be a memorable experience."


When talking with some of the other Pro players around the room, there was an interesting sentiment that arose. While they all agreed that having the events on consecutive weeks was great from a travel and community standpoint, they wished that the format could be slightly changed.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppit11/Team%20CF.JPG)*The real Team ChannelFireball, not to be confused with a bunch of guys who just bought the shirts...*
"The only problem I have with the way it is right now is that I wish it could be reversed, having the Pro Tour the week before the Grand Prix," said Luis Scott-Vargas, taking a short break from Drafting during his byes. "It can just be kind of difficult for those of us who have to prepare for both the Pro Tour and the Grand Prix. Since the Pro Tour has more at stake for us, I wish that we could devote all the time prior to it to preparing for it. If there's a Grand Prix before too, especially one of a different format, I have to put in time on that as well, and splitting attention like gives only a week of hardcore testing leading into the Pro Tour."


He wasn't entirely alone in that sentiment. When I posed the same question to Brian Kibler, who is famous for making long, globetrotting trips to Asia and Europe to play on the Grand Prix circuit, he initially said the same thing as LSV.


"Yeah, I kind of wish that it was the other way around."


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppit11/kibler.JPG)*Brian Kibler's dominion is the entire world!*
After a bit of musing though, he started to change his mind.


"...though, the more I think about it, I would like to get to where I'm going, get acclimated to the time difference, and then spend the entire week before hand testing, which is effectively what I'm going to be doing this week, so maybe it isn't as bad as I thought."


One thing that they all agreed upon was that they would love to see the Grand Prix before Pro Tours be a Limited event.


"If the Grand Prix beforehand was Limited, that would be absolutely perfect," said LSV with a smile. "You can spend all your time testing the Constructed format of the Pro Tour, and, since Pro Tours are split-format events, the Grand Prix itself is like practice for the Pro Tour. That would be ideal."


Without any prompting, and in a completely different location, Kibler said the same thing when I questioned him.


In any case, it is agreed by members of the Pro community that having Grand Prix and Pro Tours on consecutive weeks and in the same area is great for the players in that area to get to interact with a large number of Pros that they wouldn't normally get to see. It helps build up the desire to play at that higher level and drives the competitive side of the game.




Saturday, 1:50 p.m. - A Single Pro Point
----------------------------------------


*by Steve Sadin* 

When you're working your way up the pro ranks, every Pro Point counts. Given the way that the [Pro Players Club](http://archive.wizards.com/Magic/Magazine/Article.aspx?x=protour/playersclub/guidelines) is structured, just one point can be worth thousands of dollars in appearance fees, free flights, and hotels.


The hunt for Pro Points leads top players like Paulo Vitor Dama da Rosa, Yuuya Watanabe, Martin Juza, and Brian Kibler to travel all over the globe to compete in every Grand Prix that they reasonably can.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppit11/juza%20nate.jpg)*Martin Juza*
But before you can collect big checks just for showing up at events, you need to lock up your invitations to all of the Pro Tours. A win, or even "just" a Top 16 can put a player a long way towards accomplishing that goal. But sometimes a player doesn't even need to do that well. Sometimes a player just needs a single Pro Point to level up, and kick their Pro Tour career into high gear.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppit11/nelson.JPG)*Will Brandon Nelson get the Pro Point he needs this weekend?*
Well, that's just the position that Brandon Nelson (no relation to reigning Pro Tour Player of the Year Brad Nelson) finds himself in this weekend. A Top 4 finish at US Nationals left Midwestern PTQ Veteran Brandon Nelson with 14 Pro Points, and an invitation for Worlds in San Francisco. While most players would (understandably) be quite envious of Nelson's current position – he has a chance to make things way better for himself.


A Top 64 finish this weekend will earn Brandon Nelson $200 dollars and, far more importantly, his 15th Pro Point of the season. With 15 Pro Points, Brandon Nelson will reach Level 3 in the Pro Players Club – earning himself a free invitation for any Pro Tour this year and next year... an invitation that he could (and would) cash in at Pro Tour Philadelphia next weekend. Between the four points that Nelson would be guaranteed to receive just by showing up at Philly, and at Worlds in San Francisco, he would need only one additional Pro Point to reach Level 4 – insuring himself invitations to every Pro Tour in 2012 in the process.


Will Brandon Nelson earn that Pro Point that he desperately needs? Or will he find himself faced with a somewhat tougher road the rest of this season on his quest to reach Level 4?


Follow along all weekend long to find out!




Saturday, 3:00 p.m. - Quick Questions
-------------------------------------


*by Nate Price*

**What is the Best Sideboard Card in Standard Right Now?**


|  |  |
| --- | --- |
|  |  |
| **Brian Kibler** – "I don't know...[Timely Reinforcements](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Timely+Reinforcements)? It's definitely the most powerful. Though...I *do* have an [Urabrask the Hidden](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Urabrask+the+Hidden) hiding in my sideboard..." | **David Sharfman** – "I'd say [Torpor Orb](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Torpor+Orb) because it shuts off the most decks. [Memoricide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Memoricide) is definitely more powerful, but the decks are being built right now so that it doesn't just end games anymore." |

Round 4: Feature Match - Ali Aintrazi vs. Robert van Medevoort
--------------------------------------------------------------


*by Steve Sadin* 

Reigning US National Champion, and StarCityGames columnist Ali Aintrazi began making waves last year when by tearing up tournaments with his Blue-Green Turbo Land deck. Since then, Aintrazi has established himself as one of the premier rogue deck designers in the game, consistently putting up finishes with brand new decks than go on to become metagame staples.


Sitting across the table from Aintrazi this round is Grand Prix Rotterdam 2009 finalist Robert van Medevoort. A man who is known throughout the Pro community for his loud shirts, and his quiet (but deadly) play.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppit11/Robert1.jpg)*He's screaming, but only your eyes can hear him.*
While the Dutch Pro **Magic** contingent was once amongst the most dominant forces on the Pro Tour – their ranks have thinned a bit in the past few years. During this time, it's been up to Robert van Medevoort, and his good friend (and Hall of Famer) Bram Snepvangers to carry the torch for the Netherlands – a task that they have happily accepted.


 


### Game One


Medevoort kept his opening hand, while Aintrazi mulliganed to six, then agonized for a bit before keeping a hand with five lands and a [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak).


Aintrazi whiffed on a turn three [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek) that revealed a hand of two [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod)s, a [Solemn Simulacrum](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Solemn+Simulacrum), and a bunch of lands. Aintrazi allowed both of Medevoort's [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod)s to resolve, but countered the Dutch pro's [Acidic Slime](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Acidic+Slime).


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppit11/Ali2.jpg)*With only one Mana Leak to work with, Aintrazi decided to let both Pods resolve.*
Medevoort's [Solemn Simulacrum](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Solemn+Simulacrum) resolved, and was immediately upgraded into an [Acidic Slime](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Acidic+Slime) that kept Aintrazi a land short from being able to cast the [Consecrated Sphinx](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Consecrated+Sphinx) that was sitting in his hand.


Over the next two turns, Medevoort upgraded a [Viridian Emissary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Viridian+Emissary) into a [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch) while Aintrazi used a couple of [Into the Roil](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Into+the+Roil)s to bounce Medevoort's two [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod)s.


In response to Medevoort re-casting a [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod), Aintrazi (who had no interest in seeing a [Wurmcoil Engine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wurmcoil+Engine) or a titan on his opponent's side of the board) used a [Go for the Throat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Go+for+the+Throat) to kill [Acidic Slime](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Acidic+Slime).


A second [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch) came down at the end of Aintrazi's turn – and Medevoort, no doubt hoping that Aintrazi was out of answers, went to enchant a [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) onto one of his [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch)s. However, Aintrazi was ready with a second [Go for the Throat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Go+for+the+Throat).


Medevoort went for his [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) combo again the next turn... but Aintrazi's third Go For the Throat again stopped Medevoort from attacking for a million damage.


Aintrazi resolved a [Consecrated Sphinx](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Consecrated+Sphinx), but Medevoort's fourth [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch) left Aintrazi with only one untapped land and no way to prevent his opponent's third attempt at creating an infinite number of 1/4s with [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) plus [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch).


Robert van Medevoort 1 – Ali Aintrazi 0


 


### Game Two



![Thrun, the Last Troll](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Thrun%2C+the+Last+Troll)

Both players kept their opening hands for the second game, and Medevoort got off to a fast mana start with two copies of [Birds of Paradise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birds+of+Paradise). A [Viridian Emissary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Viridian+Emissary) got countered, but Aintrazi could do nothing to stop Medevoort's turn three [Thrun, the Last Troll](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thrun%2C+the+Last+Troll).


Fortunately for Aintrazi, Medevoort had no follow-up plays for several turns.


By the time Medeveoort cast his next spell, [Solemn Simulacrum](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Solemn+Simulacrum) – Aintrazi was ready with a [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak). A Go For the Throat, and a [Doom Blade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Doom+Blade) on two copies of [Birds of Paradise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birds+of+Paradise) left Medevoort with only three mana, and a long way to go before he could even think about being able to resolve his [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) combo.


Aintrazi, not wanting to give Medevoort any time to get back into the game, resolved a [Grave Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grave+Titan), and followed it up with a second [Grave Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grave+Titan) a turn later.


Medevoort copied a [Grave Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grave+Titan) with a [Phantasmal Image](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phantasmal+Image) to attempt to buy himself some breathing room, but Aintrazi's [Liliana Vess](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Liliana+Vess) was more than enough to seal the game for the reigning US National Champion.


Robert van Medevoort 1 – Ali Aintrazi 1


 


### Game Three


Medevoort kicked things off in the third game with a [Birds of Paradise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birds+of+Paradise), and a [Viridian Emissary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Viridian+Emissary) – while Aintrazi's turn two [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek) took a [Phantasmal Image](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phantasmal+Image) out of a hand that also contained [Thrun, the Last Troll](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thrun%2C+the+Last+Troll), [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin), and [Inferno Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inferno+Titan) but no lands.


Medevoort failed to draw the third land he needed to cast [Thrun, the Last Troll](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thrun%2C+the+Last+Troll) – prompting Aintrazi to untap and use a [Go for the Throat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Go+for+the+Throat) on a [Birds of Paradise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birds+of+Paradise) to further Medevoort's mana problems.


This play immediately paid off as Medevoort drew his third land, but was still a mana short from being able to cast [Thrun, the Last Troll](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Thrun%252C%2Bthe%2BLast%2BTroll).



![Creeping Tar Pit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Creeping+Tar+Pit)

Aintrazi cast a [Jace Beleren](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace+Beleren) then thought for a moment before deciding to use his planeswalker's -1 ability drawing himself a card, but letting it die to an attack from [Viridian Emissary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Viridian+Emissary).


[Liliana Vess](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Liliana+Vess) got [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak)ed, but Medevoort had no lands or spells to run out against his tapped out opponent.


An [Into the Roil](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Into+the+Roil) with kicker left the mana-light Medevoort without a single threat on the board – and gave Aintrazi a chance to draw some cards with his [Jace Beleren](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace+Beleren).


An end of turn [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch) got [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak)ed, and Medevoort finally drew a fourth land... but unfortunately for him it was a [Raging Ravine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Raging+Ravine), one of only a handful of come into play tapped lands in his deck, so he still couldn't cast the [Thrun, the Last Troll](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Thrun%252C%2Bthe%2BLast%2BTroll) that had been in his hand since the opening stages of the game.


At this point Aintrazi began attacking with his [Creeping Tar Pit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Creeping+Tar+Pit)s, and Medevoort was finally able to cast his uncounterable, Hexproof 4/4. A couple of [Creeping Tar Pit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Creeping+Tar+Pit)s swung in to leave Medevoort on 8.


Medevoort got in an attack with his [Thrun, the Last Troll](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Thrun%252C%2Bthe%2BLast%2BTroll) to leave Aintrazi on 8, but a [Despise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Despise) showed Aintrazi that the path was clear and a [Sorin's Vengeance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sorin%27s+Vengeance) allowed him to take the match.


Final Result Ali Aintrazi 2 – Robert van Medevoort 1




Round 4: Feature Match - Zohar Bhagat vs. Christian Calcano
-----------------------------------------------------------


*by Jacob Van Lunen* 

Christian Calcano is an up and coming player on the Pro Tour. Calcano managed to reach Level 4 in the Pro Player's Club during his Rookie Season last year and has begun to really put his invitations to use, finishing in the money at nearly every Pro Tour that he competes in.


Zohar Bhagat, champion of Grand Prix Minneapolis in 2009, is a CMU alum that's visiting Pittsburgh to defend the title.


Both players engaged in some friendly chat while shuffling up for the first game.


### Game One


Calcano, playing Blue Black Control, led things off with an [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek) and it became clear that Bhagat was battling with an exciting Red-White Aggro deck.


A [Grim Lavamancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grim+Lavamancer) was answered with [Doom Blade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Doom+Blade), but a top-decked [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Squadron+Hawk) refilled Bhagat's hand and gave the CMU alum an immediate board presence. Over the next few turns, the [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Squadron+Hawk)s began mounting up – Calcano was patient, however, waiting a few turns before casting a [Black Sun's Zenith](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Black+Sun%27s+Zenith) that successfully dealt with three of the birds.


Calcano looked to be in control of the game, but Bhagat found a [Goblin Guide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Guide) to join the final bird and enter the fray. Calcano casually found a land on the top of his library and cast a [Go for the Throat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Go+for+the+Throat). A [Sword of Body and Mind](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Body+and+Mind) was responded to with a [Doom Blade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Doom+Blade).


Calcano tried to close out the game with a [Consecrated Sphinx](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Consecrated+Sphinx), but Zohar had a [Dismember](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dismember) and [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt) to deal with the end game monstrosity. Calcano cast a [Jace Beleren](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace+Beleren) and drew a card, but Bhagat found a [Goblin Guide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Guide) and sent it in with a sword.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppit11/Calcano1.jpg)*Christian Calcano is trying to stave off the aggressive Red White brew being played by Zohar Bhagat.*
Bhagat made a token and milled Calcano for ten. Calcano found a [Grave Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grave+Titan) and instantly took control back. A [Mirran Crusader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mirran+Crusader) from Bhagat was unblockable, though, and Calcano's life total couldn't take the hit. Calcano looked for the Black Sun-Zenith on top of his deck, but he didn't find it. He shrugged and they were on to game two.


Zohar Bhagat 1 – Christian Calcano 0


 


### Game Two


Both players went down to six cards. Calcano nodded, "friendly game."


Bhagat started things with a [Goblin Guide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Guide), but Calcano had a [Mental Misstep](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mental+Misstep).


Bhagat had the turn two [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Squadron%2BHawk) again, while Calcano had a [Jace Beleren](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace+Beleren) that he used to draw a card. Bhagat mounted the pressure with a pair of [Mirran Crusader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mirran+Crusader)s, and Calcano used an [Into the Roil](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Into+the+Roil) plus [Despise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Despise) to deal with one. Calcano, however, was still stuck taking hits from [Mirran Crusader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mirran+Crusader), a pair of [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Squadron%2BHawk)s, and a [Grim Lavamancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grim+Lavamancer).


Calcano resolved a [Consecrated Sphinx](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Consecrated+Sphinx) after plucking an [Oblivion Ring](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oblivion+Ring) from Bhagat's hand with a discard spell. Bhagat attacked with [Mirran Crusader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mirran+Crusader), and Calcano blocked with [Consecrated Sphinx](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Consecrated+Sphinx). After combat, Bhagat used his [Grim Lavamancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grim+Lavamancer) to finish off the card advantage monster, but not before Calcano had managed to draw two extra cards with it.


Bhagat's extra [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Squadron+Hawk)s, and the [Grim Lavamancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grim+Lavamancer) were enough to dwindle down Calcano's life total. Calcano cast a [Preordain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Preordain) to dig, and drew more cards with an extra copy of [Jace Beleren](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace+Beleren), but he couldn't find a [Consume the Meek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Consume+the+Meek) or a Black Sun's Zenith to stop his opponent from pecking him to death.


**Zohar Bhagat 2 – Christian Calcano 0**


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppit11/Zohar2.jpg)*Zohar plans to get aggressive this weekend with his powerful red white deck!*

Round 5: Feature Match - Gavin Verhey vs. Eric Froehlich
--------------------------------------------------------


*by Nate Price* 

As the players sat down in the feature match area, the first thing Gavin Verhey said to me was, "I should've known. As soon as I saw my opponent, I knew there was a chance we might end up in the Feature Match area."


When I told him that our other option was the Matt Nass/Luis Scott-Vargas match that I chose not to cover because I thought they were playing identical decks, Froehlich chimed in with a smile.


"Yeah, but they're playing it in two completely different ways. I'm not going to say who's on the higher level, though. I don't want to give away the team's secret."


Froehlich started off with a quick mulligan, while Verhey stuck with his initial seven. Froehlich made a first-turn [Grim Lavamancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grim+Lavamancer), and the little Wizards started swinging as early as the next turn. A [Goblin Wardriver](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Wardriver) joined him on the following attack, but Verhey stopped the [Grim Lavamancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Grim%2BLavamancer) with a painful [Dismember](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dismember) for one and four life. Verhey dropped to 12. After combat, Froehlich added an [Ember Hauler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ember+Hauler) to his team and passed the turn. A [Mirran Crusader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mirran+Crusader) tried to jump in the way at some point, but a [Staggershock](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Staggershock) hit not only the [Crusade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crusade)r, but Verhey as well. Verhey made a [Hero of Bladehold](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hero+of+Bladehold) to try and give him something to stem the bleeding, but a [Hero of Oxid Ridge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hero+of+Oxid+Ridge) from Froehlich made his attack lethal, ending the game after a mere five minutes.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppit11/fm5%20Froehlich.jpg)*As fast as Froehlich ended the first game, maybe we should make \*his\* nickname 'The Black Mamba!'*
Gavin Verhey 0 – Eric Froehlich 1


### Game Two


This was going to be a match where things changed drastically after the first game. Hiding in Verhey's sideboard were sure to be copies of [Timely Reinforcements](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Timely+Reinforcements), which many of the Pro players I talked to agreed was the most powerful sideboard card in the format. Against the sheer aggression of Froehlich's deck, the [Reinforcements](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Reinforcements) would give Verhey some much needed life gain, as well as a few men to stymie Froehlich's attackers. It's the perfect answer card in a matchup like this.


Froehlich started fast again this game, getting a first-turn [Goblin Guide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Guide), but Verhey answered with a [Kor Firewalker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kor+Firewalker), devastating against Froehlich's mono-red deck. Fortunately, Froehlich had a [Shrine of Burning Rage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Shrine+of+Burning+Rage), providing him a colorless way to kill the Firewalker. Verhey made a [Sword of Feast and Famine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Feast+and+Famine), but he would have to wait a turn to equip it. The proved problematic for Froehlich, who needed to get rid of the Firewalker, and fast. All he could do was recruit an [Ember Hauler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ember+Hauler) to put his Shrine up to two counters and pass the turn.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppit11/fm5%20verhey.jpg)*This may be the scariest photo of Gavin Verhey in history.*
Verhey had the window he needed since he was on the play, and was able to untap and equip his Firewalker. After swinging, he made a second copy thanks to the help of a [Phantasmal Image](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phantasmal+Image). After some thought, Froehlich used his Shrine to kill the copy and attacked for six thanks to a [Teetering Peaks](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Teetering+Peaks). Verhey swung back with his equipped Firewalker, following that up with a [Gideon Jura](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gideon+Jura). After only a few seconds of thought, Froehlich packed it in for game three.


Gavin Verhey 1 – Eric Froehlich 1


### Game Three


While it wasn't the [Timely Reinforcements](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Timely+Reinforcements) that ultimately won that game for Verhey, it *was* because of the power of his sideboard. The [Kor Firewalker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kor+Firewalker)s serve double duty against Froehlich's mono-red deck, filling the exact same role as the [Reinforcements](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Reinforcements), giving him life and an infinite blocker. Even better, the protection from red keeps the [Kor Firewalker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Kor%2BFirewalker%2B)  around much longer than the tokens from [Timely Reinforcements](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Timely+Reinforcements).


Once again, Froehlich started off with a hasty [Goblin Guide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Guide). Verhey used a [Preordain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Preordain) to peek at his top cards, eventually sending a [Phantasmal Image](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phantasmal+Image) and, surprisingly, a [Timely Reinforcements](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Timely+Reinforcements) to the bottom of his deck. Froehlich slowed up on the next turn, failing to make a second-turn play. The Guide just bashed in again and provided Verhey with a second [Tectonic Edge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tectonic+Edge). On the following turn, when Froehlich tried to make a [Goblin Chieftain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Chieftain), Verhey was ready with a [Flashfreeze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flashfreeze). Verhey dropped to 12. He made a [Mirran Crusader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mirran+Crusader) to shore up his defenses, but again Froehlich had a [Staggershock](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Staggershock) to get rid of it, clearing the way for an attack. Verhey was dropping, first to 10, then to 8.


"I liked it better when he was revealing lands," Verhey admitted after revealing two consecutive [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Squadron+Hawk)s.


Froehlich then added a [Shrine of Burning Rage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Shrine+of+Burning+Rage) and a [Goblin Wardriver](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Wardriver), which Verhey quickly stopped with [Flashfreeze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flashfreeze). When the Guide attacked and revealed a *third* [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Squadron+Hawk), Froehlich just had to laugh.


"Come on! *Three* [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Squadron+Hawk)s? Unreal," Verhey said shaking his head. He dropped to 6.


Verhey's [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Squadron+Hawk)s started making their appearance over the next turns. He also bounced the [Shrine of Burning Rage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Shrine+of+Burning+Rage) with an [Into the Roil](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Into+the+Roil) before it could kill him. With two [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Squadron%2BHawk)s in play, at 6 life, Verhey tapped on the top of his deck after Froehlich attacked.


"What do you think this one is," Verhey asked Froehlich.


"Another [Dismember](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dismember), I'm hoping," he responded.


Verhey slowly flipped the top card of his deck over to reveal...[Timely Reinforcements](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Timely+Reinforcements).


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppit11/fm5%20reinforcements.JPG)*Timely indeed!*
Knowing what that help was on the top of his deck, Verhey blocked safely, keeping himself alive. After combat, Froehlich added the [Shrine of Burning Rage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Shrine+of+Burning+Rage) and a second copy of [Ember Hauler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ember+Hauler) to his board. Verhey drew his savior and made three 1/1s, gained 6 life up to 12, and cast a [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Squadron+Hawk). Froehlich thought for a minute about what to do before attacking with his [Goblin Guide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Guide). Verhey thought right back, eventually using two of his tokens to trade with the Guide. The revealed card was [Sword of Feast and Famine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Feast+and+Famine), and it immediately made it into play and onto Verhey's [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Squadron%2BHawk). He attacked with it, dropping Froehlich to one card in hand.


At this point, Froehlich tipped his plan. He used his last card, a [Combust](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Combust), to clear the last of the [Reinforcements](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Reinforcements) away and put his Shrine up to three counters. It ticked up to four during his upkeep. He attacked with his two [Ember Hauler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ember+Hauler)s, dropping Verhey to eight. All it took from that point was sacrificing the two Haulers and the Shrine and Verhey went from a relatively safe 12 to 0 in one turn. Guess those [Reinforcements](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Reinforcements) were a little late after all.


**Gavin Verhey 1 – Eric Froehlich 2**




Round 7: Feature Match - Lucas Blohon vs. Yuuya Watanabe
--------------------------------------------------------


*by Nate Price* 

You know, we've made a pretty big deal about the fact that there is a Pro Tour just down the interstate next weekend. Matches like this are why. For those who follow the Pro Tour, Lucas Blohon is probably not a new name to you. Behind Martin Juza, Blohon is probably the second most recognizable Czech player on Tour. He doesn't make it out of Europe for Grand Prix incredibly often, unless the Pro Tour happens to take him to a Grand Prix happening around the same time, just like this one. His opponent, Yuuya Watanabe, has started to travel to events more frequently since winning the Player of the Year race in 2009. Despite this, this is a match that we would commonly only get a chance to see at the Pro Tour.


### Game One


Blohon tried for a first-turn [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek), bit Watanabe had a [Spell Pierce](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Pierce) to protect his hand. He attempted a [Blade Splicer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blade+Splicer) as the first creature to hit the board, and Blohon allowed it, but used [Doom Blade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Doom+Blade) to kill the Golem before the end of Watanabe's turn. The Czech player made a [Jace Beleren](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace+Beleren) and immediately dropped it to two loyalty to draw a card. Watanabe dropped it further with an attack from the Splicer, forcing Blohon to allow Watanabe to draw a card as well to keep the planeswalker alive.


Watanabe made a [Sword of Feast and Famine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Feast+and+Famine) while Blohon was tapped out for his Jace, and he finally found a chance to equip it on the following turn. Blohon waited until Watanabe equipped it and attacked before using [Into the Roil](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Into+the+Roil) to send the Sword back to Watanabe's hand. After replaying it, Watanabe tried to attack Jace to finish it off but Blohon had an [Into the Roil](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Into+the+Roil) to send the Splicer packing. Unable to replay it, Watanabe passed the turn.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppit11/fm7%20watanabe.jpg)*Watanabe proves that 'your turn, buddy' is the same in every language.*
With the window clear, Blohon used a [Despise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Despise) to strip the Splicer from a hand that had an [Into the Roil](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Into+the+Roil), [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak), and a second copy of [Sword of Feast and Famine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Feast+and+Famine). An [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek) stripped the [Into the Roil](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Into+the+Roil) from his hand soon after. That left both players with little business in their hands, but Blohon clearly had the advantage because he had a [Jace Beleren](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace+Beleren) that had evaded all of Watanabe's attempts to destroy it.


Jace went to work. Blohon drew card after card. Watanabe decided on a path to victory, using a [Tectonic Edge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tectonic+Edge) to kill Blohon's [Tectonic Edge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tectonic+Edge), clearing the path for an [Inkmoth Nexus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inkmoth+Nexus). The Nexus picked up a [Sword of Feast and Famine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Feast+and+Famine) and started attacking. Blohon went to three poison. The Czech player tried for a [Liliana Vess](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Liliana+Vess), but the [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak) that had been in his hand the whole game stopped it from hitting play. Watanabe had added a [Blade Splicer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blade+Splicer) to his team, but he had already decided on riding the Nexus to victory. He played and equipped a [Sword of War and Peace](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+War+and+Peace), as well as the [Sword of Feast and Famine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Feast+and+Famine) in play. The Nexus took Blohon to 8 poison while the Splicer and his Golem took care of Jace.


Blohon recruited a second planeswalker, [Karn Liberated](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Karn+Liberated), to replace the fallen baby Jace. It immediately exiled the [Inkmoth Nexus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inkmoth+Nexus) that threatened to kill him. Undeterred, Watanabe took to the skies with a [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Squadron+Hawk) and friends, who, as everyone knows by now, *love* to carry Swords. Before they could do the deed, though, Blohon found his saving grace in a Black Suns's Zenith. The only creature that survived was the Golem token, which was carrying both Swords. Undeterred, Watanabe wasted no time in refilling the board with his remaining two [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Squadron+Hawk)s, and Blohon was unable to survive even two more turns.


Lucas Blohon 0 – Yuuya Watanabe 1


### Game Two


A first-turn [Despise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Despise) from Blohon ripped a [Sun Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sun+Titan) from a hand also containing [Preordain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Preordain) and five lands. Watanabe went to work, immediately thinning his deck with a [Steam Vents](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Steam+Vents) before using a [Preordain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Preordain) to filter his draws a little more. He made the first contribution to the board when he cast a [Sword of Feast and Famine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Feast+and+Famine) on his third turn, but Blohon was not far behind, casting a [Solemn Simulacrum](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Solemn+Simulacrum) immediately following that.


Watanabe took advantage of the fact that Blohon was tapped out to activate his [Inkmoth Nexus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inkmoth+Nexus), once again give it a [Sword of Feast and Famine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Feast+and+Famine), and attack the Czech player, forcing a discard and untapping his lands. To follow that, he made a [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Squadron+Hawk) and searched up a pair, revealing that he had the third in his hand. Blohon confirmed this with an [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek), which also revealed a [Jace Beleren](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace+Beleren) and a [Preordain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Preordain), the latter of which he took. Afterwards, he cast [Liliana Vess](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Liliana+Vess) and immediately gave her -2 loyalty to go fetch a card and put it on top of his deck.


Watanabe decided to equip his Sword to his [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Squadron%2BHawk), but chose not to kill [Liliana Vess](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Liliana%2BVess), going after Blohon directly instead. He used the remainder of his mana to cast the [Jace Beleren](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace+Beleren) that Blohon had been kind enough to leave him and immediately drew a card. Thanks to his Sword, he was also able to add a second [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Squadron+Hawk) to his team to provide Jace a little cover.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppit11/fm7%20Blohon.jpg)*Blohon tries desperately to find a way out of his tight spot.*
Blohon sent his [Simulacrum](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Simulacrum) at Jace, and the little [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Squadron%2BHawk) that Watanabe had left behind did its job, stepping in the way. After that, Blohon simply used [Liliana Vess](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Liliana%2BVess) to search for another card before passing the turn. Watanabe had a chance and took it, activating his Nexus to finish off [Liliana Vess](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Liliana%2BVess), as well as attacking Blohon with his equipped [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Squadron%2BHawk), knocking the searched-for [Consecrated Sphinx](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Consecrated+Sphinx) from Blohon's hand. The card Blohon had searched for the second time turned out to be [Consume the Meek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Consume+the+Meek), which Blohon used to erase all of Watanabe's creatures. He untapped and used an [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek) to reveal Watanabe's hand, and could muster nothing more than a bleak smile as he took an [Oblivion Ring](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oblivion+Ring) over an [Emeria Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Emeria+Angel) and two Swords. The next few turns were pretty straightforward as Blohon, who was out of gas, succumbed to the powerful spells that Watanabe's Jace had drawn him.


**Lucas Blohon 0 – Yuuya Watanabe 2**

----------------------------------
