Round 7: Feature Match - Gaudenis Vidugiris vs. Tom Martell
-----------------------------------------------------------


*by Steve Sadin* 

After years of near misses, Tom Martell was finally able to catapult himself into Level 5 in the Pro Players Club last year thanks in large part to a second place finish at Grand Prix Columbus. Martell made good use of his free invitation to every Pro Tour this year by starting off the season with a Top 8 at Pro Tour Paris, where he piloted the then breakout [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Squadron%2BHawk)-[Sword of Feast and Famine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Sword%2Bof%2BFeast%2Band%2BFamine) deck.


Gaudenis Vidugiris has been making his presence felt on the Pro Tour for several years now, racking up Grand Prix Top 8s, and money finishes at Pro Tours with striking regularity. This year hasn't been too bad for Vidugiris either, as he walked away from Grand Prix Denver with the trophy, and earned the first Pro Tour Top 8 of his career in Nagoya.


By the time I walked over to the table to record the match, the two long time friends and teammates were already well into a conversation that I couldn't help but try to imagine the beginning of.


"...I'm probably rooting for her, because she's never slapped me." Said the outspoken Martell.


"Wait, who slapped you?" asked Vidugiris.


"Jeeeez... how out of the loop are you?" replied Martell.


 


### Game One


Vidugiris got things started with a bunch of lands, a couple of copies of [Explore](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Explore) and a [Khalni Heart Expedition](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Khalni+Heart+Expedition) (after he had played most of his lands), while Martell spent his first couple of turns playing [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Squadron+Hawk)s, and leaving up mana in case Vidugiris tried to cast a titan or a [Oracle of Mul Daya](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oracle+of+Mul+Daya).


Despite getting off to a fast mana start, Vidugiris found himself stuck on five mana, and consequently unable to cast any of his biggest spells. Martell took advantage of his opponent's mana hiccup by drawing three extra cards with [Jace Beleren](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace+Beleren), and keeping up the pressure with his army of [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Squadron+Hawk)s.


When Vidugiris finally drew a sixth land, it was a [Valakut, the Molten Pinnacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Valakut%2C+the+Molten+Pinnacle) – a come into play tapped land that Martell immediately destroyed with a [Tectonic Edge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tectonic+Edge).


A [Rampant Growth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rampant+Growth) a turn later promised to put Vidugiris up to six mana on the following turn... but not before he died to an attack from Martell's four [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Squadron+Hawk)s and his [Celestial Colonnade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Celestial+Colonnade).


Tom Martell 1 – Gaudenis Vidugiris 0


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppit11/fm7%20Gaudenis.JPG)*Gaudenis Vidugiris*
 


### Game Two


Martell and Vidugiris spent their first few turns playing lands and passing the turn back and forth – the only thing interrupting their land playing ways was a [Rampant Growth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rampant+Growth) for Vidugiris, and a [Preordain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Preordain) for Martell. When Vidugiris had finished manually working his way to six mana, he attempted to resolve an [Inferno Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inferno+Titan) only to see it get countered by a [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak).


A second [Inferno Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inferno+Titan) a turn later got countered by a second [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak), and Vidugiris' follow up play of [Summoning Trap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Summoning+Trap) was stopped by a [Dispel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dispel).


Martell's [Torpor Orb](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Torpor+Orb) promised to make his spot removal a lot more effective – a play that immediately paid dividends when Vidugiris resolved a [Primeval Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Primeval+Titan) that Martell killed with a [Day of Judgment](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Day+of+Judgment).


[Oracle of Mul Daya](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oracle+of+Mul+Daya) dug Vidugiris into a [Valakut, the Molten Pinnacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Valakut%2C+the+Molten+Pinnacle) – but Martell had a [Tectonic Edge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tectonic+Edge) and a [Dismember](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dismember) to once again leave Vidugiris with a whole lot of lands, but no threats on the board.


Vidugiris played out a [Khalni Heart Expedition](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Khalni+Heart+Expedition), while Martell looked to put away with the game quickly with a [Sun Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sun+Titan)... but when Vidugiris's [Summoning Trap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Summoning+Trap) hit a [Primeval Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Primeval+Titan), Martell suddenly found himself in need of a miracle.


Vidugiris attacked with his [Primeval Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Primeval+Titan), and fetched two copies of [Valakut, the Molten Pinnacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Valakut%2C+the+Molten+Pinnacle), then sacrificed his [Khalni Heart Expedition](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Khalni+Heart+Expedition) to find two [Mountain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mountain)s – destroying Martell's [Sun Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sun+Titan) and dealing him 12 points of ([Valakut, the Molten Pinnacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Valakut%252C%2Bthe%2BMolten%2BPinnacle) plus combat) damage in the process.


Martell hoped that his [Oblivion Ring](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oblivion+Ring) would buy him some time, but Vidugiris had the Nature's Claim to force a deciding third game in their match.


Tom Martell 1 – Gaudenis Vidugiris 1


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppit11/fm7%20Martell.JPG)*Tom Martell*
 


### **Game Three**


 


With only 11 minutes left on the clock for the third game, the two players knew that they needed to play fast as neither of them wanted the match to end in an unintentional draw.


Martell cast a [Jace Beleren](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace+Beleren) on turn three, while Vidugiris played out an [Oracle of Mul Daya](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oracle+of+Mul+Daya). [Dismember](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dismember) killed the [Oracle of Mul Daya](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oracle+of+Mul+Daya), and a [Torpor Orb](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Torpor+Orb) gave Martell a bit of breathing room even if his opponent had a titan.


Rather than try to cast a creature, which Martell was likely to have an answer for in his hand since he had just tapped out to cast [Torpor Orb](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Torpor+Orb), Vidugiris chose to attack in with his [Raging Ravine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Raging+Ravine) to destroy Martell's [Jace Beleren](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace+Beleren).


Martell had a replacement [Jace Beleren](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace+Beleren) the next turn, but Vidugiris's [Raging Ravine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Raging+Ravine) ate that one too.


Lacking a threat of his own to cast (and fully aware of the fact that there were only 5 minutes left on the match clock so he couldn't afford to bluff that he had a hand full of answers), Martell began attacking with a [Celestial Colonnade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Celestial+Colonnade).


Martell got a couple of hits in, knocking Vidugiris down to 12, but Vidugiris used this time to build up two [Khalni Heart Expedition](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Khalni+Heart+Expedition)s which, along with a [Raging Ravine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Raging+Ravine) and a [Valakut, the Molten Pinnacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Valakut%2C+the+Molten+Pinnacle), was just enough to kill Martell before time in the round expired.


Final Result:


**Gaudenis Vidugiris 2 – Tom Martell 1**




Round 8: Feature Match - Lucas Florent vs. Jonas Köstler
--------------------------------------------------------


*by Jacob van Lunen* 

Jonas Köstler is an up and coming German pro who's been making a name for himself with some nice finishes, including a Top 8 at Grand Prix: Bochum last year. His opponent, Lucas Florent, is a French pro that is well-known for his interesting card evaluations in constructed and limited alike.


Both players are undefeated at this point and are looking to maintain their perfect Day One records.


 


### **Game One**


 


Florent, playing Blue-Black Control, led things off with a [Preordain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Preordain). Köstler tapped a [Raging Ravine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Raging+Ravine) and an [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island) to cast an [Overgrown Battlement](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Overgrown+Battlement) on turn two, but Florent had a [Doom Blade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Doom+Blade) to prevent the German from accelerating his mana.


Köstler managed to stick a second copy of [Overgrown Battlement](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Overgrown+Battlement), but it also fell at the hands of [Doom Blade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Doom+Blade) when Köstler attempted to cast yet another copy of the mana producing 0/4 wall.


Köstler kept three cards on top with [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder), and cast a [Birds of Paradise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birds+of+Paradise) before passing the turn back to Florent.


Köstler attempted a [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod), but Jonas cast a [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak). Köstler tapped his three remaining mana and resolved his artifact. Florent then made it clear why he wanted Köstler to tap out when he cast a [Grave Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grave+Titan).


Köstler calmly put a [Sea Gate Oracle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sea+Gate+Oracle) onto the battlefield and resolved the trigger. He cast his fourth [Overgrown Battlement](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Overgrown+Battlement), and used [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) to sacrifice the [Sea Gate Oracle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sea+Gate+Oracle) and make a [Phyrexian Metamorph](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phyrexian+Metamorph), which copied the [Grave Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grave+Titan).


[Grave Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grave+Titan) came into the red zone and Köstler chose to chump block it with one of his zombie tokens.


Köstler attempted an [Inferno Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inferno+Titan) and it resolved, he aimed all three damage at Florent's [Grave Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grave+Titan). [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) searched up a [Phantasmal Image](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phantasmal+Image) to copy the [Inferno Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inferno+Titan) and finish off Florent's [Grave Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grave+Titan).


Florent found no help on the top of his library and passed the turn.


Köstler tutored up a [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch) and tapped one of Florent's zombies. The two [Inferno Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inferno+Titan)s were able to split up their damage and ensure that Florent wouldn't be blocking with anyone.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppit11/DSCN0526.JPG)*Lucas Florent is trying to keep his record blemish free here in Pittsburgh.*
Jonas Köstler 1 -- Lucas Florent 0


 


### Game Two


Köstler started strong with a [Birds of Paradise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birds+of+Paradise), and an [Overgrown Battlement](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Overgrown+Battlement), while Florent simply made his land drops, and left mana open should Köstler try to cast any threats.


Florent used a [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak) to counter [Obstinate Baloth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Obstinate+Baloth), then tapped out for a [Liliana Vess](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Liliana+Vess) and made Köstler discard a card.


Köstler capitalized on Florent tapping out by casting a [Consecrated Sphinx](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Consecrated+Sphinx), which drew him two cards when Florent began his turn.


Florent answered the [Consecrated Sphinx](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Consecrated+Sphinx) with a [Consecrated Sphinx](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Consecrated+Sphinx) of his own. Each player having a Sphinx means that the draw triggers may be used off the other Sphinx's trigger. Florent chose not to draw two extra cards during Köstler's draw step because he didn't want Köstler to get new cards while he was tapped out.


Köstler already had a [Frost Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Frost+Titan), though, which opened up a path for [Consecrated Sphinx](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Consecrated+Sphinx) to attack [Liliana Vess](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Liliana+Vess).


Köstler chose not to draw off his [Consecrated Sphinx](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Consecrated+Sphinx) during Florent's draw step. Florent used the -2 ability on [Liliana Vess](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Liliana+Vess) to put a mystery card on top of his library before passing the turn with a bunch of mana untapped.


Köstler attacked to kill the [Liliana Vess](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Liliana%2BVess) and deal Florent six points of damage. He decided to draw some cards during Florent's draw step, but Florent had found the [Go for the Throat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Go+for+the+Throat) and used it on his opponent's [Consecrated Sphinx](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Consecrated+Sphinx), ensuring that he could safely draw four new cards.


Florent found a bunch of lands in those four cards and was forced to pass the turn.


Köstler let Florent draw some cards off his [Consecrated Sphinx](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Consecrated+Sphinx) and continued to apply pressure with his [Frost Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Frost+Titan). Florent still hadn't found a removal spell in the six cards he had drawn off his [Consecrated Sphinx](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Consecrated+Sphinx).


Florent drew a [Go for the Throat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Go+for+the+Throat), and cast [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek) to see what Köstler might be sitting on. Köstler showed him an [Acidic Slime](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Acidic+Slime). Florent passed the turn after casting his [Go for the Throat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Go+for+the+Throat).


Köstler's [Acidic Slime](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Acidic+Slime) destroyed a land, but Florent answered with a [Jace Beleren](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace+Beleren). He drew a card and passed the turn.


Köstler tried to mount an offense, but Florent's [Consecrated Sphinx](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Consecrated+Sphinx) began getting out of hand and, with little time left on the clock, Köstler decided to concede after Florent cast [Karn Liberated](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Karn+Liberated).


Jonas Köstler 1 – Lucas Florent 1


 


### Game Three


Florent decided to go down to six cards when his hand didn't have a reasonable answer for [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod). Köstler kept his opening seven.


Köstler started the game with an [Overgrown Battlement](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Overgrown+Battlement) which he used to ramp into a [Solemn Simulacrum](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Solemn+Simulacrum) on the following turn.


Florent continued playing lands until his fourth turn, when he tapped out to cast [Foresee](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Foresee).


Köstler took advantage of the fact that his opponent had tapped out to resolve a [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) that he immediately used to turn his [Solemn Simulacrum](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Solemn+Simulacrum) into an [Acidic Slime](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Acidic+Slime), which destroyed one of Florent's lands.


Florent had no play other than a [Preordain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Preordain), allowing Köstler to upgrade his [Acidic Slime](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Acidic+Slime) into a [Frost Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Frost+Titan) that locked down another one of Florent's lands.


Florent went to [Doom Blade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Doom+Blade) Köstler's [Frost Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Frost+Titan), but Köstler had a [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak) at the ready. A couple of attacks, and [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) Activations later and Jonas Köstler had won the match.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppit11/DSCN0527.JPG)*Jonas Köstler remains undefeated in the Steel City!*
**Jonas Köstler 2-1 Lucas Florent**




Round 9: Feature Match - Ben Stark vs. Mat Marr
-----------------------------------------------


*by Nate Price* 

This is it. With one more match to play before the end of Day one, both Mat Marr and Ben Stark had their backs against the wall. Sitting at 6-2, both players were a single win away from making Day two. Unfortunately, they were also one loss away from watching Day two from the sidelines. There was some banter back and forth between both players as they discussed the upcoming week and the Pro Tour next weekend. If nothing else, these two have quite an interesting history against each other.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppit11/r9%20bags.jpg)*Pictured: Ben Stark and Mat Marr's bags. Not pictured: Ben Stark and Mat Marr.*
"I'd say that whoever wins this match has to win the tournament, but I don't think we're 100% on that anymore, are we," observed Mat Marr as the players were shuffling up for the first game.


"No we still are. Both of the matches I've played you and beat you, I've gone on to win the tournament," Stark corrected him.


"Oh yeah, I guess the streak's still alive then," Marr said with a laugh.


Marr started off with a mulligan, prompting a short discussion on mulligans at the Pro Tour and how Stark wishes that we could track the number of times players mulligan at the Pro Tour. By the time Marr made his second play, a [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Squadron+Hawk), Stark started to laugh.


"Looks like we traded decks from the last time we played each other," he said between chuckles.


A [Rampant Growth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rampant+Growth) fetching a [Mountain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mountain) from him told of a [Valakut, the Molten Pinnacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Valakut%2C+the+Molten+Pinnacle) in Marr's future. Marr went right back to the game plan, playing a [Sword of Feast and Famine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Feast+and+Famine), which he no doubt intended to give to his [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Squadron%2BHawk). I have heard that this is a potent strategy.


Stark used a pair of [Explore](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Explore)s to explode up to six mana, though he had yet to do anything productive with it. Marr just pressed on, equipping his [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Squadron%2BHawk), attacking, and playing another pair, careful to leave mana available to represent [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak).


After untapping, Stark paused for some thought. He had accelerated himself into six mana, but now he had to do something and his opponent was signaling [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak). He chose to attempt an [Oracle of Mul Daya](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oracle+of+Mul+Daya). Marr asked him if he had made a land drop before allowing the Oracle to hit play. Stark immediately revealed a land, which he put into play, turning the top of his library into a [Summoning Trap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Summoning+Trap). Stark then used an [Explore](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Explore) to draw the Trap, revealing an [Inferno Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inferno+Titan) underneath. Marr filled the skies with the remainders of his [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Squadron%2BHawk)s, attacked, and passed the turn, still with only four lands in play.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppit11/r9%20marr.jpg)*Mat Marr knows there's a burning around the corner, but he has to get his Hawks down if he wants to win.*
Stark drew his [Inferno Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inferno+Titan) and played it, killing the three unequipped [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Squadron%2BHawk)s on Marr's side. He then tricked out the top of his deck by sacrificing an [Evolving Wilds](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Evolving+Wilds), which got him a [Valakut, the Molten Pinnacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Valakut%2C+the+Molten+Pinnacle). With five [Mountain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mountain)s in play, each one from this point would be an uncounterable [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt). It wasn't able to stick around long, though, as Marr quickly dispatched it with a [Tectonic Edge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tectonic+Edge), dropping to three lands to do so. A [Timely Reinforcements](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Timely+Reinforcements) got Marr a trio of blockers, but the [Inferno Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inferno+Titan)'s triggered ability roasted them when he attacked. A second Titan came down the turn after, cooking the equipped [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Squadron%2BHawk) and leaving the board bare. One more attack and the game was over.


Ben Stark 1 – Mat Marr 0


### Game Two


Both players kept their opening draws for the second game, though Marr's was with a fairly pained expression on his face. The second game started out not too dissimilarly from the last, with Stark using [Rampant Growth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rampant+Growth) and [Oracle of Mul Daya](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oracle+of+Mul+Daya) to accelerate his mana while Marr set up a [Sword of Feast and Famine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Feast+and+Famine) and a [Phantasmal Image](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phantasmal+Image) to copy Stark's Oracle. Stark had a second Oracle, but Marr had a pair of [Dismember](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dismember)s to kill them and drop himself to twelve life. With the Image unable to hold a Sword, Marr finally turned to the skies, recruiting a [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Squadron+Hawk), equipping it, and filling up his hand.


Aaand then the [Inferno Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inferno+Titan) hit. One damage scared the Image away, one went to the [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Squadron%2BHawk), and the last went to Marr. After that, Stark used a [Nature's Claim](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nature%27s+Claim) to kill the Sword, killing the [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Squadron%2BHawk) carrying it in the process. Marr drew his card, gave it a strange look, and then commented, "I have no idea why I boarded this card in." That card was [Elesh Norn, Grand Cenobite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elesh+Norn%2C+Grand+Cenobite). While it shrunk the [Inferno Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inferno+Titan), it didn't shrink his ability. When Stark swung in on the following turn, he used it to force Marr to make the trade with his Elesh Norn. When Stark made an [Avenger of Zendikar](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Avenger+of+Zendikar) and filled his board with tokens, Marr just nodded, "Oh yeah, that's why." Stark played an [Explore](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Explore) to cycle into a card and then laughed. He revealed his hand of two [Verdant Catacombs](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Verdant+Catacombs), which supercharged his Plants, killing Marr and advancing to Day two.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppit11/r9%20stark.jpg)*If history has told us anything, we should just give him the trophy now.*
"Congratulations," Marr offered him. "Keep the streak alive."


**Ben Stark 2 – Mat Marr 0**




Round 9: Feature Match - Eric English vs. Gerry Thompson
--------------------------------------------------------


*by Steve Sadin* 

Long time pro, writer, and deck builder extraordinaire Gerry Thompson has spent the better part of this year dominating the StarCityGames Open Series. He now finds himself in a very familiar situation – playing a match to go undefeated on Day One of a Grand Prix.


For Eric English, being at the top tables of a premier event is a new experience. The recent Cornell graduate began playing competitively during Llorwyn block, and has since made the Top 8 at five of the ten PTQs that he's played in.


The bad news for English? He's failed to convert on any of his five Top 8s.


The good news? He's now 8-0, and in a great position to earn his first invitation to the Pro Tour.


 


### **Game One**


 


A [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder), and a [Shrine of Piercing Vision](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Shrine+of+Piercing+Vision) promised to smooth out English's draws, while a [Jace Beleren](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace+Beleren) gave Thompson a way to generate some actual card advantage which would come in handy in what would undoubtedly be a long, drawn out game...


Or English could play an end of turn [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch), untap, enchant it with a [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) and win the game on his fourth turn.


Eric English 1 – Gerry Thompson 0


### Game Two


"You're going to Top 8 this tournament for sure" said Thompson.


"You're killing me. Now I feel like I'm under all this pressure to do well," replied English humbly.


"No, you're killing me! Literally!" said Thompson.


 


### Game Two


A turn two [Torpor Orb](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Torpor+Orb) for Thompson meant that English would need to work a bit harder to combo off this time around than he did in


### Game One


 .![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppit11/r9%20GerryT.jpg)*Gerry Thompson*
English tried to stick a [Grim Lavamancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grim+Lavamancer) with [Dispel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dispel) for backup, but Thompson had two [Mental Misstep](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mental+Misstep)s to keep the little wizard off the board.


English's [Spellskite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spellskite) died to a [Dismember](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dismember) – but with the [Dismember](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dismember) out of the way, English felt safe to cast a [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch).


A couple of turns, and a couple of scratches from [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch) later, Thompson tapped low for an [Emeria Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Emeria+Angel) that English countered with a [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak).


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppit11/r9%20English.jpg)*Eric English*
English untapped, and decided that he was ready to go for it. [Steel Sabotage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Steel+Sabotage) bounced [Torpor Orb](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Torpor+Orb), and then English attempted to put a [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) on his [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch).


Thompson tried to bounce the 1/4 with an [Into the Roil](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Into+the+Roil), but English had the [Negate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Negate) to protect his combo and allow himself to end Day One with a flawless 9-0 record.


**Eric English 2 – Gerry Thompson 0**
